- The provided working directory is the only submission surface for this evaluation.

## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# CockroachDB Raft Consensus and Lease Management Cross-Component Discovery

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in cockroachdb/cockroach under pkg/kv/kvserver/ that implement the Raft consensus integration and range lease management. Identify: the Replica.handleRaftReady method and its state machine application, the Store.processReady batch processing, the lease request and transfer logic (RequestLease, TransferLease), the lease expiration vs epoch-based lease types, and the liveness-based node health checking that feeds into lease decisions. Report each file path and key function or type.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/cockroach--v24.3.0.

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

In cases where the leaseholder crashes, we must wait for\\n176: \\t\\t\\t\\t// raft to elect a new leader before any other replica (typically the\\n177: \\t\\t\\t\\t// new leader) can determine the (in)validity of the old lease and go on\\n178: \\t\\t\\t\\t// to replace it.\\n179: \\t\\t\\t\\tknownSuccessor := i.RaftStatus.Term > lease.Term && i.RaftStatus.Lead != raft.None\\n180: \\t\\t\\t\\tif !knownSuccessor {\\n181: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tstatus.State = kvserverpb.LeaseState_ERROR\\n182: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\tstatus.ErrInfo = \\\"leader lease is not held locally, cannot determine validity\\\"\\n183: \\t\\t\\t\\t\\treturn status\\n184: \\t\\t\\t\\t}\\n185: \\t\\t\\t\\t// We know of a newer raft leader. We still don't know the exact extent\\n186: \\t\\t\\t\\t// of the leader support that the lease had, but we know that leader\\n187: \\t\\t\\t\\t// support has either already expired or was never even established due\\n188: \\t\\t\\t\\t// to a failure of the raft leader to fortify. Either way, the leader of\\n189: \\t\\t\\t\\t// lease.Term cannot think this lease's leader support is in the future.\\n190: \\t\\t\\t}\\n191: \\t\\t}\\n192: \\tdefault:\\n193: \\t\\tpanic(\\\"unexpected lease type\\\")\\n194: \\t}\\n195: \\texpiration := status.Expiration()\\n196: \\tmaxOffset := i.MaxOffset\\n197: \\tstasis := expiration.Add(-int64(maxOffset), 0)\\n198: \\townedLocally := lease.OwnedBy(i.LocalStoreID)\\n199: \\t// NB: the order of these checks is important, and goes from stronger to\\n200: \\t// weaker reasons why the lease may be considered invalid. For example,\\n201: \\t// EXPIRED or PROSCRIBED must take precedence over UNUSABLE, because some\\n202: \\t// callers consider UNUSABLE as valid. For an example issue that this ordering\\n203: \\t// may cause, see https://github.com/cockroachdb/cockroach/issues/100101.\\n204: \\tif expiration.LessEq(i.Now.ToTimestamp()) {\\n205: \\t\\tstatus.State = kvserverpb.LeaseState_EXPIRED\\n206: \\t} else if ownedLocally && lease.ProposedTS.Less(i.MinProposedTs) {\\n207: \\t\\t// If the replica owns the lease, additional verify that the lease's\\n208: \\t\\t// proposed timestamp is not earlier than the min proposed timestamp.\\n209: \\t\\tstatus.State = kvserverpb.LeaseState_PROSCRIBED\\n210: \\t} else if stasis.LessEq(i.RequestTs) {\\n211: \\t\\tstatus.State = kvserverpb.LeaseState_UNUSABLE\\n212: \\t} else {\\n213: \\t\\tstatus.State = kvserverpb.LeaseState_VALID\\n214: \\t}\\n215: \\treturn status\\n216: }\\n217: \\n218: var leaseStatusLogLimiter = func() *log.EveryN {\\n219: \\te := log.Every(15 * time.Second)\\n220: \\te.ShouldLog() // waste the first shot\\n221: \", \"url\": \"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/cockroach--v24.3.0@2e3aaf185d0ed9361efdbf04cd7cd1153477d912/-/blob/pkg/kv/kvserver/leases/status.go%3FL100-220\"}, \"isError\": false}"

CockroachDB v24.3 supports three lease types: expiration-based (LeaseExpiration), epoch-based (LeaseEpoch), and leader-based (LeaseLeader, new). The desired type is chosen per-replica by desiredLeaseTypeRLocked. Lease acquisition is initiated by requestLeaseLocked \u2192 pendingLeaseRequest.InitOrJoinRequest, which proposes a RequestLease Raft command. Cooperative transfers use AdminTransferLease \u2192 TransferLease command.\",\n\n    \"lease_types\": {\n      \"LeaseExpiration\": {\n        \"roachpb_constant\": \"roachpb.LeaseExpiration\",\n        \"description\": \"Valid while wall_time < lease.Expiration - max_clock_offset. Also used when kv.expiration_leases_only.enabled is true.\",\n        \"validity_check\": \"status.Expiration() compared to now; stasis period = expiration - max_clock_offset\"\n      },\n      \"LeaseEpoch\": {\n        \"roachpb_constant\": \"roachpb.LeaseEpoch\",\n        \"description\": \"Does not expire by wall clock. Each node heartbeats a liveness record (stored in KV near the start of the keyspace) using conditional puts. The liveness record contains an epoch and an expiration timestamp.
